text:
My Family has been making this for years and years. One way to avoid having to refridgerate it over night is to lay each side of the graham cracker squares in milk for a few seconds until slightly soft, right before laying them on the cake. This keeps them moist and it's ready to serve right then. We used our own topping instead of the frosting: 3T Butter, 3T. Hot water, 3T Cocoa powder and about 1 and 1/2 cup powdered sugar (to desired thickness)Just pour over the top. This creates a thin layer of chocolate and makes it much more elegant in my opinion!

text:
I'm giving this 4 stars b/c I thought it was ok, but my guests loved it.  I had a version of this before that was absolutely delicious, but I don't think this recipe was as good.  Part of it may be that it was barely fridged for 4 hours, so possibly if it had "sat" longer, it would've tasted better.  I also used cinnamon graham crackers b/c that's all I had, and I personally didn't like the cinnamon flavor in the cake, but other people thought it was a great touch.  I think some great variations would be to make it like tiramisu with some coffee flavoring, b/c overall it just tasted plain to me - sweet - but plain in flavor.  The version I had eaten before had vanilla and chocolate layers.  I may try that next time, maybe even add some coffee into the mix.
UPDATE:
I made a variation with chocolate graham crackers and Fat/sugar free cheesecake pudding w/ dark chocolate frosting.  It was REALLY good.  The tip to heat up the frosting is a must since it's SO much easier that way and you end up getting a nice smooth, shiny coating just like an eclair.  Also, I would recommend making this in a big rectangular tupperware so that you can just snap the lid on top.  I kept finding my saran wrap would "suction" itself to my frosting when I made it in a pan and not look as pretty.  It's also essential to let the cake sit for at least overnight.  This version sat for 2 days and the texture was just WAY better than the first one I made which barely sat for 4 hours as the recipe stated.

text:
Wow, this is so sinfully delicious!  This was my second time making it, and I'm glad I did because the first one I made was not that great.  My family and I thought the store-bought frosting I put on the first one was way too sweet, as well as way too much.  Also, I used cheesecake flavored pudding on the first one and we didn't really care for that flavor either.  This time I decided to use the vanilla flavor pudding (as per recipe) and make a chocolate ganache for the topping.  OMG heaven!!  I made it the night before to allow the flavors to set and took it to a potluck at work.  Everyone was fighting over the leftovers & they all wanted the recipe.  I cannot begin to describe how delicious this is for such a simple dessert (took less than 10 minutes to put together).  I think the ganache is what really made the difference this time.  (2/3 cup heavy whipping cream brought just to a boil, then pour over 1 cup semi-sweet chocolate chips...I used Ghirardelli, whisk until smooth and pour over cake.  Then allow to refrigerate overnight to set.)  You have to try this recipe...trust me, you won't be disappointed!

text:
Although this is not a gourmet dessert, it gets 5 stars because it's so easy, tasty and a real crowd pleaser. I followed some other reviewers' advice: Used French vanilla pudding to make cake and put in the fridge for a few hours prior to adding topping.  Then made a simple ganache using 2/3 cup heavy cream and 1 cup semi-sweet chocolate chips.  Don't be afraid of the word "ganache"---just let heavy cream come to a boil and then pour over chips in bowl. Let sit for one minute and stir until smooth.  Cool slightly and pour over cake.  It will seem liquidity but thickens nicely after refrigerating overnight. Really very little work and a huge improvement over store bought frosting.  And definitely refrigerate overnight---4 hours does not allow enough time for crackers to soften and flavors to meld.  Also, it's easy to cut and presents nicely when it's made well in advance.

text:
I love homemade whipped cream and frosting so much more than the store bought kind, so I made the recipe a little more complicated.  I used non-fat milk, homemade whipped cream, and I made ganache for the frosting which I spooned over the cake before the ganache got a chance to harden.  I mashed up the graham crackers and added melted butter to form a crust just because I like graham cracker crust more than graham crackers.  For the second and third graham cracker layers I just sprinkled the graham cracker and butter crumbles.  The cake is delicious after a few hours of chilling (we couldn't wait till the next day) but it doesn't hold together well until a full night in the fridge.  I read the recipe wrong and only put in 1 box of pudding mix and so it was a little thin.  But sooo fab!  Thanks for the great idea! :)(For the ganache I whisked in about 9 oz of Nestle Toll House mini semi-sweet chocolate chips to 1 cup of gently boiling heavy whipping cream but I had way too much frosting left over, so next time I'll reduce it or make something else to put the frosting on.)

text:
I've made this for both home and office parties and everyone loves it.  However the "ready" time is far too short.

1.  If using a disposable cake pan you will need more than 1 box of graham crackers.  It will take about 1 more package of crackers.
 
2.  Because the pudding mixture thickens so very quickly, open the graham crackers packages and put on a tray, etc so you can quickly grab and place them.  If you don't, by the time you get to the second layer the pudding mix will be difficult to pour.
 
3.  Using a wisk, quickly mix the pudding and milk for a few seconds and then add the cool whip continuing to mix.  Make sure the cool whip is completely mixed in.  
 
4.  Microwave the icing (I use Betty Crocker creamy chocolate) for about 30 seconds, stir and then pour over the top layer of crackers.

5.  Give the graham crackers time to soften.  If making for lunch or dinner, make cake the night before.
 
I haven't tried it yet but was thinking that this might be good with a chocolate pudding/cool whip mixture for the filling with vanilla icing as the topping.

text:
So easy to make, a friend made this for a party and everyone loved it so now I make it, and its easy to make and take.  However, instead of the canned icing she made ganache and I prefer it that way.   I cup of cream brought almost to a boil, pour it over 1 cup of bittersweet chocolate that has been chopped and allow it to soften for a minute, then whisk.  Let it set 10 minutes to cool and thicken, then pour it over.  See Eclair Cake with Chocolate Ganache on this site for the Ganache recipe if needed.

text:
I was pleasantly surprised to see this recipe here! My aunt made this cake at a family get-together about 7 years ago, and I have made it many times since. It is always a hit and completely disappears! However, our family's recipe doesn't call for the third cup of milk, only the 2 cups needed to prepare the instant pudding according to the pudding box directions. I might try it with the third cup.   Also, the chocolate frosting spreads easier if you microwave the container for 30-45 seconds (be sure to remove the aluminum film from the container entirely, because you don't want metal sparking in the microwave). Then stir the frosting with a spoon or knife, pour it over the pie, and spread. Then I refrigerate it at least 4 hours, but really this dish is best the 2nd and 3rd days, if it lasts that long!

text:
I've been making this dessert for at least 10 years and it's always a huge success.  My recipe is a tiny bit different..  I use French vanilla pudding and add 1 t. of vanilla to the filling.  If you use canned frosting that you nuke slightly it is much easier to frost.  And it is absolutely necessary to refrigerate overnight if you want good results.  For special occasions I make a HUGE cream puff with a hole in the center.  I cut it in half horizontally and then add the filling.  I believe that's where the name came from as the original recipe did call for a cream puff instead of graham crackers.  Made this way it would look more like an Ã©clair and knocks people off their feet!

This was a hit at the super bowl party.  I beg to differ with reviewers, this tasted very much like the choco covered eclairs I buy in the freezer section.  The graham crackers I bought were store brand, not very sweet and tasted like cardboard to me.   But I had to use them since I bought them especially for this. Poured over and smoothed out and put in the fridge for 24 hours.  AMAZING!!!!

text:
This recipe is an oldie, but a goody! You can play around with ingredients and have a whole different, but still super easy and delicious dessert! I sometimes use Oreo's in place of the graham crackers - yummy! I have also used vanilla wafers and banana pudding, ginger snaps and cheese cake pudding, chocolate chip cookies with a layer of vanilla and a layer of chocolate pudding, - all super delicious. The trick is to let this sit over night whatever combo you use. It allows the moisture in the pudding to infuse into whatever cookie or cracker you use so they become soft and oh so scrumptious! Enjoy!!

I made this twice. The first time I bought vanilla cook and serve pudding thinking it was instant. Then after waiting 24 hours and cutting into it, the cake was liquified. The next day I remade it using a layer of cheesecake instant pudding on the bottom and a layer of banana cream instant pudding on the top. Yummy! My husband thought it tasted like a donut. text:
Frosting tip,  blend nutella, cool whip and caramel syrup ......... begin in a bowl of course and make in small amounts, adjusting the ingredients to your taste preference. Before refrigerating, top the cake with half of the frosting mixture, saving the remaining frosting in the cool whip container to top the cake before serving. That way you have no worries of the saran or foil affecting the frosting appearance.

I made this for my mother's birthday, and it was a hit!  Delicious!
I also used one package regular vanilla, and one french (that's all they had left at the store!), and it turned out great.
I also dipped the graham crackers in milk first, as someone suggested.
Oh, I did use a recipe for the chocolate, which ended up going with the rest of it GREAT.
2 cups powdered sugar
3/4 cup unsweetened cocoa powder
1/3 cup milk
1/4 cup butter, melted
1 teaspoon vanilla extract

text:
I fixed this for a housewarming party and it was a crowd pleaser. Everyone wanted the recipe. It was very easy to make and I wasn't in the kitchen very long. I did have to add at least another 1/2 cup of milk for a smoother texture. One great tip for this recipe is to put your store bought chocolate frosting in the microwave for about 30-35 seconds. After    mixing the chocolate  I just poured it on top of the eclair cake. I didn't even have to spread it with a knife. I will be making the recipe many, many more times.

text:
I like this recipe for several reasons. Not only is it the easiest thing in the world to make, it's one dessert that appeals to both adults and kids (there aren't too many of those!) I use the French vanilla pudding and add a little extra vanilla. Also, if you microwave the icing (as suggested by some of the reviewers), not only is it easier to spread but you can just get a thin "glaze" on top instead of a thick coating (which is what you want in an "eclair.") Haven't met anyone yet who doesn't love it!!

BIG FAT YUM!  I made this today to take to friends' house tomorrow because I heard that it is even better the next day.  I don't know, but it sure was INCREDIBLE today!  Just a couple tips others have suggested.  I used my kitchen aid mixer with the whisk attached to mix the cool whip, milk and pudding.  I let it set in the fridge for just a couple minutes. text:
This went over big with my family and so easy.  I followed the recipe to the letter with the exception of adding a tsp. of vanilla extract to the pudding mixture and letting the cracker/pudding layers set in the refrigerator for about 2 hours before frosting (I used milk chocolate), which, upon the tips of others here, I heated at 80 power for 30 seconds then stirred.  This made it quite easy to spread over the top cracker layer.  I refrigerated it for a full 7 hours before cutting.  Quite pretty.  I will be making this again.  Thanks for sharing.

text:
The first time I made this, my colleagues liked it but I  thought it had too much of an "instant/out of the box" taste.  I tweaked this by adding bananas (ripe but still firm) and folding in natural peanut butter (about 1/2 to 3/4 cup, depending how strong you want the PB taste to be) into the pudding and whipped topping mix.  And instead of packaged frosting, I make a quick ganache--8 oz chocolate melted in 8 oz hot cream for the full recipe. I now call it "banana refrigerator cake" and actually prefer it to banana cream pie because it's less sweet.

It's amazingly simple but it tastes phenomenal!! My family didn't believe that it needed no baking. 

They don't sell graham crackers where I live (Sad, huh?) so I used ladies' finger cookies instead. I sliced them lengthwise and layered them with the cream. If you let it sit for 1-2 days, it tastes just like cake!!

Another thing I changed was I omitted the milk altogether and used real vanilla pudding (not the mix! those that come in the snack cups) instead. Just mix the pudding with the whipped cream and voila! A perfect cream for layering.

I made this Monday night for dinner on Tuesday and was a bit skeptical because I didn't have a chance to test it out beforehand.  But everyone loved it and raved about it.  The person I was most worried about was my boyfriend because he doesn't like mushy desserts (eg. tiramisu) and he loved it the most! I used cinnamon graham crackers and vanilla pudding (I wanted to use white chocolate but they only had sugar free) and canned frosting.  I didn't find the dessert sweet at all except for the frosting.  In fact, I will use only half a can next time because I had some left over and thought there was too much on top.  Oh and I also nuked the can in the microwave to make spreading easier.  Very quick and easy dessert and I like that I can play around with the flavours.  Thanks for the recipe!

text:
This is absolutely heavenly and SO simple to make!! I used french vanilla pudding and added just a touch of vanilla extract to the pudding mixture. I also followed the advice of a couple of other reviewer's and dipped the graham crackers in milk before putting in the cake and they were nice and soft after only refrigerating for 4 hours, but not mushy the next day (This only lasted 2 days in our house!!). Lastly, I put the chocolate frosting in the microwave for 45 seconds, which made it very easy to just pour on top. Delicious!!

text:
The recipe as is, is okay, but I didn't really think it tasted like an eclair. I experimented a bit and made some variations which I think really improved on it and resulted in an eclair taste. Instead of using graham crackers I used crushed vanilla wafers for the bottom and middle layers. The top layer I used crushed chocolate wafers. For the filling I only used 2 cups of milk as it made the filling a little more thicker and flavorful. I folded in the Cool Whip after I thoroughly mixed the milk and pudding together. I used a milk chocolate frosting on top, but only used about 1/2 of the container so it would just have a thin layer on top and like other reviewers microwaved it for about 30 seconds so it became a glaze and was easy to pour and spread. It was so much better. Both times I did use the Cool Whip, but next time I will use my homemade whipped cream as I prefer it to Cool Whip and I think will enhance the flavor even more.

We loved this recipe.  It did taste a lot like an eclair!  My 3 year old son actually did most of the work...very easy and loved that it is no-bake.  Great for summer barbeques. Made my own fudge icing, which hardedned nicely in the fridge and then softened slightly at room temp: 1cup sugar, 1/2 cup cocoa powder, 1/2 cup milk, 4 tbsp butter, 2 tbsp lt corn syrup, dash of salt.  Boil together in saucepan 3 minutes,then add 1 tsp vanilla and 3/4 to 1 cup powdered sugar.  it will pour right over the cake.  will definately make this again for a crowd!

text:
I scaled this down to make in a 9x9 pan-a 6 serving package of pudding, 2 1/3 cups milk, 3/4 of the container of whipped topping, enough graham crackers to cover the pan, and what was left of a can of chocolate frosting, which I heated in the microwave and poured over.  It was much more reasonable for two people, although I've been eating it for four days and it gets better the longer it sits.  Also, next time I'll splurge on brand-name graham crackers, since it took forever for mine to get soft.  
For people who substituted sugar free pudding and tried to match the number of ounces, I think it's easier to match the serving size or it will be too stiff.

I first ate this several years ago, and made it soon after from memory based off what the woman who made it told me.  I never wrote it down, and ended up forgetting what was in in. text:
I've made this recipe many many times but I've tweeked it a bit:
1. Since I strongly dislike frosting, I buy a large bar of milk chocolate (a good quality is best). I break it into pieces and melt it in the microwavable bowl with a splash of canola oil. I heat at 5-10 second intervals (stirring in between). Then, I drizzle the melted chocolate on top of the final layer of the eclair. It hardens into perfection.
2. I make 5-6 layers instead of the three that's called for in this recipe.
3. The graham crackers can be replaced with plain tea biscuits. They are cheaper than and taste the same, if not better. :)

I used 2% milk. 2 containers of STORE brand topping that looks like cool whip but I did use good gram crackers.  I made in the large square aluminum pan i got from the 99 cent store.  no spraying anything at the bottom I saw those on some recipes and why? your not baking anything. text:
I seriously could not believe how delicious this was.  I made it 24 hours in advance of serving it (a must, so the graham crackers absorb the pudding and convert to the consistency of crust).  Wow.  Unbelievable.  It reminded me of a cream-filled maple bar (donut).  I used homemade chocolate frosting (softened in the microwave to a pourable consistency).  As the frosting cools in the fridge, it takes on the appearance/consistency of a ganache.  Next time, I plan to use a dark chocolate ganache.  Whipped this whole thing up in literally minutes.  A thousand "thank you's" for the recipe.

I made this cake twice in one week and I was intent in producing a rich, creamy dessert.   Both times I used homemade ganache topping and I used whole milk for the pudding.  I did use whipped topping as the recipe called for.  The first cake had 9 hours to soften and comingle flavors.  It was very good but the graham crackers were not fully softened. The second cake I made 60 hours in advance of consumption for an office lunch and it was wonderful.  This time I used semisweet chocolate.  In fact the lunch and dessert were also a competition and my Ãclair Cake won first place, out of six other desserts.   For both cakes I added a nice decorative variegated white topping (using a toothpick technique, like a spider web.  See photo.)  This is a keeper recipe!

This desert is so delicious and very easy to make.  For the chocolate frosting try the following: -1 1/2 cup milk chocolate chips -1/2 cup butter -1 cup heavy cream Mix the three ingreadients and place on the stove on low heat until chocolate melts.  I guarantee it will be the best frosting ever.  I will definately make this again.

text:
I really enjoyed this, and so did my guests.  I made some changes:  I did use a handmixer in order to get a pudding-type consistency.  I blended 3 boxes French Vanilla Instant Pudding with 4 cups very cold milk, then blended in 16 oz (2 reg. size Cool Whip) Cool Whip.  I used an entire box of graham crackers, for a total of three layers.  For the icing, I microwaved hot fudge frosting in the can until syrupy and then poured over the top.  This is best two or more days after making, so it's great to make ahead of an event in order to leave time for cleaning and preparing other foods closer to the event.  It has a very rich flavor and holds its shape well.  I might blend 1+ cup of creamy peanut butter to the pudding mixture next time for something different.  Delicious!

I used Chocolate tea biscuits - I dipped each one in a cup of hot coffee and then lined them up as the recipe calls - I used about 5 packages of those tea biscuits - on the final row, I ended up not covering it with another layer of the crackers, instead I left the pudding uncovered, and crumbled the remaining crackers and sprinkled the crumbs on top, I also added some chopped walnuts and chocolate chip cookies, and then I made zig-zag lines with Chocolate syrup (the one that you use for Ice cream) - covered it and stuffed it in the fridge over night - in the morning we had it with coffee - so delicious!

This "cake" is not special enough to make for birthdays or special events. Many reviewers suggested that they rec'd requests for birthdays, etc., and that it was a big hit. Hmm? It's not a terrible recipe, because it's easy to make and tastes good, but it's nothing great. We're talking about graham crackers and pudding, basically. This is the type of thing that is perfect to make when you're craving a dessert and have all or most of the ingredients on hand. It's perfect to half for one or two people to keep on hand to snack on. It's far from being too sweet. It's mild. As for a special occasion or to present to important company, I'd skip this one and do a little more work.

text:
I thought this was pretty good.  I used French vanilla pudding instead of the plain vanilla.  I also halved the recipe and put it into a smaller mini version of the 13x9 pan.  I am not sure what size it was but it worked out beautifully and was more than enough.  I used one 3.5 box of French vanilla pudding, 1/2 tub of 8oz fat free whipped topping and I also ended up with 3 layers instead of 2.  I put one layer of graham crackers, pudding, crackers, pudding, crackers and pudding and finally the last layer of crackers.  For the frosting, I used Baker's brand dipping chocolate and melted it as instructed and poured this over the entire dish.  It worked out really well.  I thought it was simple and good!

text:
I'm only giving this a 4 because I had an old version of the recipe that I think is better.  Try using french vanilla pudding instead of regular vanilla and always refrigerate overnight.  That will make it take exactly like an eclair.  Also, as someone else on the site noted, heat the frosting and pour it over the cake.  It will be smooth and shiny the next morning when you take it out of the fridge.  With those changes, this is a 5.

text:
To make this taste like a real eclair, use unsalted tops saltine crackers in place of the graham crackers.  Softened in the chilling process, at least overnight, and you will get a more realistic taste of eclair.  

Graham crackers are ok, but will never make it taste like an eclair.

text:
This is one of my favorite desserts ever, I made it for the first time on Valentine's Day and then just made it again this afternoon! When my boyfriend tasted it, he asked where it had been his whole life. If you have a couple extra minutes, I recommend you use the Eagle Brand Chocolate Fondue recipe from this site for the chocolate on top:  Just mix together a 14 ounce can sweetened condensed milk, 1 cup semisweet chocolate chips, 2 tablespoons butter and 2 tablespoons water in a saucepan over medium heat until the chocolate chips are melted. Remove from heat and stir in 1 teaspoon vanilla extract.  Pour over the eclair and spread with a spatula to cover everything. It's so good this way! The one I made today I used banana pudding in and it tastes good, too.

text:
Thank you so much for submitting this recipe.  I had lost mine.  The only thing that I do different is take the chocolate frosting.  Remove the lid, take off the foil and microwave for about one to two minutes or until chocolate turns liquid. Poor over cake smooth with knife then refrigerate for four to six hours so cake flavors can set. This gives it a high gloss look and makes you think of ice cream cones dipped in chocolate.  Thanks for the post, I lost mine.

This tasted pretty good. I used honey grahams, butter pecan pudding, and dark chocolate frosting from a can I melted in the micro for 30 seconds and then poured on top. I probably ended up using more coolwhip than specified, as I am metric and I never know if that sort of packaging is weight or volume, so I added coolwhip until it tasted good but wasn't too fluffy (basically aimed for the texture of my home-made pastry cream) since the cool whip is also labelled in ml's. Love this as is, but I usually make my own frosting. It tastes better, imho, and isn't much more difficult than store-bought. 2 cups confectioners (powdered) sugar, 4 T milk, 3T cocoa powder. Mix together, pour, and spread! If you want more frosting, just up everything by half, but I think it is sweet enough without more frosting. Delicious! Otherwise, I make this recipe as is. I do think it would be delicious w/coffee brushed over the Graham crackers and espresso powder in the glaze, with different flavored puddings, or with cinnamon or chocolate crackers. Yummy and versatile

This is easy and a good crowd-pleaser. I made it with chocolate pudding instead of vanilla, because that's what my kids like, and I think it was a little too much chocolate. It would have tasted more like an eclair with vanilla. I always use real whipped cream instead of Cool-Whip, I substitute 8oz/1c whipped cream and one packet of Whip-It stabilizer, optionally add a tablespoon or two of sugar when you whip it. I cut this recipe in half to make a 9" pie. I used packaged chocolate frosting because I was in a hurry, but I think next time I will make a ganache instead.

text:
I've made this cake before and love it, but I just have to say this. The suggestion to microwave the frosting for 15-30 seconds is a simple, yet genius idea. I don't make this recipe nearly as often as I like because it's incredibly difficult to frost graham crackers that are on a bed of pudding. Like, I want to poke out my eyeballs when I'm done, difficult. But the frosting softening makes it a snap, and I might be whipping this up a lot more often now. I love the eclair cake as is, but I also make a variation with chocolate Graham's, cheesecake pudding, and cheesecake frosting. Wowza!

text:
This is a great recipe that I've used to feed large crowds. My only advice is to not use store-brand ingredients. I have made with store-brand and name brand (ie; Nabisco, Jello, Betty Crocker). When made with store-brand, it really had a terrible aftertaste. Likewise with banana pudding. Use real Nilla wafers and jello pudding - you'll be much happier with the results!

text:
I tried this recipe and found it bland with the plain vanilla and the frosting was way too sweet. So I changed it a little. I swapped out one of the vanilla's for a French vanilla. I usually double the recipe making it easier. I do 2 vanilla's for a layer, 2 French vanilla's with the whipped topping mixed in, for the 2nd layer. Then instead of the frosting. I use chocolate pudding. The dark chocolate is the best but if I can't find it. I use regular chocolate. This is super simple and always a crowd pleaser. I have taken this to several potlucks and always bring 2 pans of this. Normally 1 pan is empty in no time and I am able to bring home just enough for my family of 5 to have 1 helping a piece.

This one is a keeper!! YUMMY!!
I made this dessert for my hubby's bday.
He loves Boston cream pie so I thought this 
would be to his pleasing...It sure is!!
He couldn't stop after one large serving.
And he also could not believe the recipe is semi-homemade since I usually bake from scratch.
Things I changed...  
*I used french vanilla pudding mixes.
*I topped with chocolate ganache recipe submitted by INGRIDEVOGEL via allrecipes (but I used  organic pure vanilla in place of the rum in the ganache recipe)super easy to make!!
**The last thing...I used a smaller clear casserole dish (8x10x3)approx...It made my slices of dessert more dense..If you use this smaller pan you only need about 1/2 recipe for the ganache topping.
If you are using 13x9 pan you need about 2/3 of the ganache recipe.

Love it!  This is going to be my next birthday cake even if I have to make it myself!  I have made it using French vanilla pudding and regular vanilla and prefer the flavor of the French vanilla.  I also made my own chocolate buttercream because I think most prepared chocolate frostings are gross. I have found that if I serve it too soon the graham crackers will still be crunchy and eclairs should not crunch.  Thanks for the recipe!

text:
I've been using this recipe for years (my mother passed it down to me.) It never fails to get at least one request for the recipe. If you're expecting it to taste exactly like an eclair from a bakery in cake form, you're going to be disappointed. Of course it's not going to taste just like an eclair! This is more of an imitation, simpler, poor man's eclair :) I typically go a little light on the chocolate frosting topping... preferring to drizzle rather than spread. Too much tends to make the whole cake a little too sweet.

text:
My husband really enjoyed this dessert for his birthday!! We followed the recipe except using sugar free pudding and cool whip instead of regular. One comment - if using sugar free pudding mix like we did, do not use 7 ounces total of pudding mix like the recipe calls for. This turned out to be way too much. Use 4-5 ounces instead. Ours turned out quite stiff with 7 ounces of pudding mix. Add slowly, then you can judge for yourself how much you will need.

It's hard to review this recipe, since I had it in my head this would taste like an eclair from a bakery.  While it reminds you of an eclair, it doesn't taste like one; rather it tastes exactly like what it is...a layering of store bought items: graham crackers, pudding, and a tub of frosting.  If you are looking for a recipe simple enough for a child to make that anyone would enjoy, it's great.  If you are going for a homemade dessert that looks and tastes amazing, find a recipe that starts from scratch.
